  <script type="text/javascript">//<![CDATA[
	function external_links_in_new_windows_loop() {
		if (!document.links) {
			document.links = document.getElementsByTagName('a');
		}
		var change_link = false;
		var force = '';
		var ignore = '';

		for (var t=0; t<document.links.length; t++) {
			var all_links = document.links[t];
			change_link = false;
			
			if(document.links[t].hasAttribute('onClick') == false) {
				// forced if the address starts with http (or also https), but does not link to the current domain
				if(all_links.href.search(/^http/) != -1 && all_links.href.search('optimwise.com') == -1) {
					// alert('Changeda '+all_links.href);
					change_link = true;
				}
					
				if(force != '' && all_links.href.search(force) != -1) {
					// forced
					// alert('force '+all_links.href);
					change_link = true;
				}
				
				if(ignore != '' && all_links.href.search(ignore) != -1) {
					// alert('ignore '+all_links.href);
					// ignored
					change_link = false;
				}

				if(change_link == true) {
					// alert('Changed '+all_links.href);
					document.links[t].setAttribute('onClick', 'javascript:window.open(\''+all_links.href+'\'); return false;');
					document.links[t].removeAttribute('target');
				}
			}
		}
	}
	
	// Load
	function external_links_in_new_windows_load(func)
	{	
		var oldonload = window.onload;
		if (typeof window.onload != 'function'){
			window.onload = func;
		} else {
			window.onload = function(){
				oldonload();
				func();
			}
		}
	}

	external_links_in_new_windows_load(external_links_in_new_windows_loop);
	//]]></script>

   <div class="page-title">
    <div class="wrap">
     <h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">Copy &amp; Migrate WordPress Sites with Duplicator Plugin</h1> 
    </div>
   </div>
   <div class="site-inner">
    <div class="content-sidebar-wrap">
     <main class="content" id="genesis-content">
      <div class="breadcrumb" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/BreadcrumbList">
       You are here: 
       <span class="breadcrumb-link-wrap" itemprop="itemListElement" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/ListItem"><a href="https://optimwise.com/" itemprop="item"><span itemprop="name">Home</span></a></span> 
       <span aria-label="breadcrumb separator">/</span> 
       <a href="https://optimwise.com/blog/">WordPress Maintenance &amp; Tips Blog</a> 
       <span aria-label="breadcrumb separator">/</span> Copy &amp; Migrate WordPress Sites with Duplicator Plugin
      </div>
      <article class="post-2455 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail category-websites tag-backup tag-plugin tag-wordpress tag-wordpress-maintenance entry gs-1 gs-odd gs-featured-content-entry" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/CreativeWork">
       <header class="entry-header">
        <p class="entry-meta"><time class="entry-time" itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2012-09-19T11:00:27+00:00">September 19, 2012</time> | <span class="entry-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"><span class="entry-author-name" itemprop="name">Chad Warner</span></span> <span class="entry-comments-link"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comments">222 Comments</a></span> </p>
       </header>
       <div class="entry-content" itemprop="text">
        <p>The free <a href="https://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/duplicator/">Duplicator plugin</a> makes it easy to copy and migrate WordPress sites. It’s the best free alternative I could find to <a href="http://ithemes.com/member/go.php?r=44922&amp;i=l44">BackupBuddy</a>, (aff. link) the extremely popular backup and migration plugin from iThemes.</p> 
        <p><em>Note: this post was first written in 2012. We&nbsp;currently use <a href="https://managewp.com/?utm_source=A&amp;utm_medium=Link&amp;utm_campaign=A&amp;utm_mrl=2860">ManageWP</a> (aff. link) for migrating sites, but we still use Duplicator in some cases where ManageWP won’t work (such as sites that aren’t publicly accessible). Despite this post’s&nbsp;age,&nbsp;people still find&nbsp;it&nbsp;useful.</em></p> 
        <p>Here’s how to make a copy of your site with Duplicator. The exact steps you follow may differ depending on your server/host.</p> 
        <p>Note: you <em>don’t</em> need to install WordPress at the destination before following these steps.</p> 
        <h2>Create a Copy of the Website</h2> 
        <ol> 
         <li>Install and activate <a href="https://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/duplicator/">Duplicator</a>.</li> 
         <li>In your admin menu, you’ll have a new Duplicator menu item. Click it.</li> 
         <li>Click the <strong>Create Package</strong> button, then <strong>Create Package Set</strong>.</li> 
         <li>If you’re moving to another server, click the <strong>Installer</strong> and <strong>Package</strong> buttons to download the files. If you’re staying on the same server, skip to the next step.</li> 
         <li>Use FTP or another file manager to access your website. If you downloaded the installer and package, upload them to the directory where your new site will live. If you’re staying on the same server, notice the&nbsp;new <em>wp-snapshots</em> directory next to your <em>wp-admin</em> and <em>wp-content</em> directories. Copy the files ending <em>installer.php</em> and <em>package.zip</em> to the directory where your new site will live. Rename the file ending <em>installer.php</em> to simply <em>installer.php</em>.</li> 
        </ol> 
        <p><a href="http://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-package-set.png"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2459" title="Duplicator plugin package set" src="http://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-package-set.png" alt="Duplicator plugin package set" width="776" height="79" srcset="https://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-package-set.png 776w, https://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-package-set-300x31.png 300w, https://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-package-set-768x78.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 776px) 100vw, 776px"></a></p> 
        <h2>Create a New Database</h2> 
        <p>The Duplicator plugin is supposed to be able to create databases, but I couldn’t get it to work, so I manually create them. If you need to do this, see your host for instructions (BlueHost and HostMonster users, see <a href="https://my.bluehost.com/cgi/help/6">MySQL Database Creation</a>)</p> 
        <ol> 
         <li>In cPanel, create a new database.</li> 
         <li>Create a new database user.</li> 
         <li>Give the user all privileges to the database you created.</li> 
        </ol> 
        <h2>Install the Package</h2> 
        <ol> 
         <li>In your browser, enter the URL of the new website, followed by <em>/installer.php</em>. For example, if I’m creating dev.optimwise.com, I’d browse to <em>dev.optimwise.com/installer.php</em>.</li> 
         <li>Change the fields in the <strong>Settings</strong> section if desired.</li> 
         <li>Enter the database information, and click <strong>Test Settings</strong>.</li> 
         <li>Check the box <strong><label for="accept-warnings">I have read all warnings &amp; notices</label></strong>.</li> 
         <li>Click <strong>Install</strong> and wait for the installation.</li> 
         <li>Follow the steps on the next page to finish the installation.</li> 
         <li>Delete the contents of <em>wp-snapshots</em> in the source site.</li> 
        </ol> 
        <p><a href="http://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-installer.png"><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2461" title="Duplicator plugin installer" src="http://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-installer.png" alt="Duplicator plugin installer" width="703" height="417" srcset="https://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-installer.png 703w, https://optimwise.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Duplicator-plugin-installer-300x178.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 703px) 100vw, 703px"></a></p> 
        <p>For more details, see the <a href="http://support.lifeinthegrid.com/knowledgebase.php?article=3">User Guide at LifeInTheGrid.com</a> (the plugin author’s site). Here’s the official overview video:</p> 
        <p><iframe width="500" height="281" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/yZ7pHmR9JC8?feature=oembed" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe></p> 
        <h2>Troubleshooting</h2> 
        <p>If Duplicator doesn’t work the first time you run it, try again. Sometimes it works the second time.</p> 
        <p>Duplicator may not be able to create packages for sites with a lot of content; it may time out. Try going into the Duplicator settings and excluding <em>wp-content</em>. After using Duplicator to migrate the package, manually move <em>wp-content</em> via SFTP.</p> 
        <p>Duplicator should automatically change your links to reflect your new site URL. If you have problems, you may need to refresh your permalinks. In your WordPress admin menu, go to <strong>Settings</strong> &gt; <strong>Permalinks.</strong> Your current selection should already be selected; just click <strong>Save Changes</strong> without changing anything.</p> 
        <p>Since I didn’t create this plugin, and haven’t used it in all its possible ways, I haven’t experienced many of the problems that others have. So, I’m not the best person to ask for support. I suggest that you ask in the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/plugin/duplicator" rel="nofollow">Duplicator plugin’s support forum</a>, <a href="https://lifeinthegrid.com/support/" rel="nofollow">LifeInTheGrid support</a> (they make the Duplicator plugin), or the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/" rel="nofollow">general WordPress.org Support Forums</a>.</p> 
        <p>If you need <strong>professional help migrating or copying</strong> your WordPress site,&nbsp;<a href="http://optimwise.com/contact/">please contact us</a>.</p> 
        <h2>Pro Version</h2> 
        <p>If you like the free version of Duplicator, you may be interested&nbsp;in <a href="https://snapcreek.com/duplicator/?wpo-premium">Duplicator Pro, an enhanced version</a> which adds scheduled cloud backups and several other new features. We haven’t used it, but it’s worth checking out.</p> 
        <h2>Express Your Gratitude</h2> 
        <p>If this plugin worked for you, please consider <a href="http://lifeinthegrid.com/partner/">donating to support the developer</a> (which isn’t&nbsp;me). After all, how much time and money did this free plugin save you?</p> 
        <h2>Let OptimWise Maintain Your WordPress Site</h2> 
        <p>You’d rather manage your business than manage your WordPress site. At OptimWise, we know how to take care of WordPress sites for businesses. We’ve been doing it since 2010!&nbsp;<a href="https://optimwise.com/services/wordpress-maintenance-service/">Sign up for your WordPress Maintenance Plan today</a>.</p>

          </div>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1452"> 
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment">

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>Hi,</p> 
           <p>Thanks for the clear instructions. But i had 2 warnings at the end. The problem now is that i can’t upload and files/pictures/plugins at my Xampp backup. Could someone help me out ?<br> Thanks</p> 
           <p>WP-CONFIG WARNING: The wp-config.php has one or more of these values “WP_CONTENT_DIR, WP_CONTENT_URL, WPCACHEHOME, COOKIE_DOMAIN, WP_SITEURL, WP_HOME, WP_TEMP_DIR” which may cause issues please validate these values by opening the file<br> .<br> MEDIA SETTINGS WARNING: The table ‘wp_options’ has at least one the following values [‘upload_url_path’,’upload_path’] set please validate settings. These settings can be changed in the wp-admin by going to Settings-&gt;Media area see ‘Uploading Files</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1474#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1474&quot;, &quot;1474&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Maikel">Reply</a>

         <ul class="children"> 
          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1475"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-08-02T07:17:29+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1475" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">August 2, 2013 at 7:17 am</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Maikel, sorry to hear that you had issues. I haven’t used Duplicator for local installations such as Xampp, so I don’t have any specific advice. It sounds like some of the paths changed when you went to/from Xampp. For the first warning, check your wp-config.php file. You may want to compare it to a copy of the file from a clean installation of WordPress. For the second warning, go into your WordPress admin and check Settings &gt; Media to see if it has an upload path specified. Otherwise you may need to look at that in the database, in the wp-options table.</p> 
             <p>If you can’t figure it out, you may need to find someone familiar with using Duplicator and Xampp. You could ask in the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/plugin/duplicator" rel="nofollow">Duplicator plugin’s support forum</a>, <a href="https://lifeinthegrid.com/support/" rel="nofollow">LifeInTheGrid support</a> (they make the Duplicator plugin), or the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/" rel="nofollow">general WordPress.org Support Forums</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1475#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1475&quot;, &quot;1475&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Chad Warner">Reply</a>
            </div>

            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Kim, I just recently purchased BackupBuddy (after writing this post), and I’ve only used it for backups so far; not for migration. From what I’ve read, the migration functionality is very similar. The only limitation I’ve run into with Duplicator was in duplicating a site that was over 2 GB, on a shared host. The process kept timing out. I ended up using the Duplicator settings to exclude the wp-uploads directory, and moved that directory via SFTP instead.</p> 
             <p>You may be able to find a more detailed comparison elsewhere.</p> 
             <p>Yeah, <a href="http://2013.grandrapids.wordcamp.org/" rel="nofollow">WordCamp Grand Rapids</a> should be a great time!</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">

          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor even depth-2" id="comment-1485"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-08-19T15:01:14+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1485" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">August 19, 2013 at 3:01 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Amy, to update your permalinks means to log into WordPress, then go to Settings &gt; Permalinks. Your current selection should already be selected; just click Save Changes without changing anything. That step is often required when making changes to WordPress (after migrations, after creating custom post types, etc.). If you changed your permalink structure, try changing it back to what you had. If that doesn’t work, you may need to run Duplicator again, this time simply saving the permalinks as they are, rather than changing them.</p> 
            </div>

           <ul class="children"> 
            <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor even depth-3" id="comment-1488"> 
             <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
              <header class="comment-header"> 
               <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
               <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-08-20T07:54:15+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1488" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">August 20, 2013 at 7:54 am</a></time></p> 
              </header> 
              <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
               <p>Emilio, I haven’t tried to store the package on an external server, but I very much doubt that’s an option. Once I had a site that had so much content that Duplicator was choking, so I went into the Duplicator settings and excluded <em>wp-content</em>. The package was much smaller. After migrating, I manually moved <em>wp-content</em> via SFTP. You could try that if you’re running out of space.</p> 
               <p>Other than that, try asking for help in the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/plugin/duplicator" rel="nofollow">Duplicator plugin’s support forum</a>, <a href="https://lifeinthegrid.com/support/" rel="nofollow">LifeInTheGrid support</a> (they make the Duplicator plugin), or the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/" rel="nofollow">general WordPress.org Support Forums</a>.</p> 
              </div> 
              <div class="comment-reply">
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1488#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1488&quot;, &quot;1488&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Chad Warner">Reply</a>

           <p>Hi, I followed all instructions and everything seemed to work fine, but none of my files actually transferred to my new site. I never got any errors, there just nothing at the new site. I checked my download and it has everything in it. What could have happened?</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1493#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1493&quot;, &quot;1493&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Mike Lawrence">Reply</a>

         <ul class="children"> 
          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1494"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-09-12T17:51:28+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1494" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">September 12, 2013 at 5:51 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Mike, I’d first say try again. When others have had issues, they’ve repeated the process and it worked the second time. If that doesn’t work, read on. When you say there’s nothing at the new site, what do you mean? When you browse to your address, do you just get a white screen? If so, it may be an issue with the theme. Try to go straight to your login page (domain.com/wp-login.php) and see if you can get to the admin area. If you can, try switching themes. It could also be a plugin issue. You can deactivate plugins by renaming their directories. </p> 
             <p>If none of this helps, try asking for help in the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/plugin/duplicator" rel="nofollow">Duplicator plugin’s support forum</a>, <a href="https://lifeinthegrid.com/support/" rel="nofollow">LifeInTheGrid support</a> (they make the Duplicator plugin), or the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/" rel="nofollow">general WordPress.org Support Forums</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">

           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/4ee8eb9ea464174ad52e0385e8373a7a?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/4ee8eb9ea464174ad52e0385e8373a7a?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name">Troy</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-09-16T13:45:50+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1497" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">September 16, 2013 at 1:45 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>Hi Chad – thanks for this great post.<br> I’m a very fresh-off-the-press newbie and have just completed my wife’s first WP business website. My problem: due to unforeseen circumstances, I have to move her site from the current host to a new host. I would like to keep all of her MySQL and WordPress settings (ie. user names, passwords, database name, table prefix, host name … etc) all exactly the same on the new host, as what I had set up on the old host. Just checking with you – that if I follow all your instructions and fill in all the same details in the new setups as I did in the old – that all will be fine?<br> Thanks again ?</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-reply">

         <ul class="children"> 
          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1498"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-09-16T14:53:47+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1498" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">September 16, 2013 at 2:53 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Troy, the Duplicator plugin should handle that just fine. It packages up the MySQL database and all the files (WordPress core and user uploads), then lets you move them to a new location and unpack them. The site’s settings are included in either the database or the files (such as wp-config.php), so they’ll all migrate. </p> 
             <p>Note that the new host may a have different database hostname than your old host; you’ll need to check. When you create your new database on the new host, you should be able to use the same name as on the old host, and the table prefix will be preserved by Duplicator.</p> 
             <p>The nice thing is, the package is just a copy of your site, so if by chance something doesn’t work right, you can always try again; your original site will not be affected in the process.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1498#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1498&quot;, &quot;1498&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Chad Warner">Reply</a>
            </div> 
           </article> </li> 
         </ul> </li>

          <header class="comment-header"> 
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/5df19293bd928209e657c5d21642be7a?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/5df19293bd928209e657c5d21642be7a?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="https://gravatar.com/megancarroll" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">megancarroll</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-09-23T16:43:55+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1501" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">September 23, 2013 at 4:43 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>Chad, I have an existing WordPress site that I need to redesign and I am wondering if you can help me figure out how to go about it. The new website I am building is going to be very different than the old one (totally new design, new pages, new categorization system, etc.). The problem is that my client wants to retain all of the blog posts (incl. photos) and user information from the old site. </p> 
           <p>I’ve been doing some reading, but it seems like the more reading I do, the more confused I get. Is the following the correct way to go about this?</p> 
           <p>(1) Use Duplicator to clone the site to a new location (say, example.com/newsite). (2) Use the duplicate site as a dev environment to build a custom theme, create the new pages, and reorganize the categories, while keeping the old site live at example.com. (3) When the new site is ready, move the installation from example.com/newsite to example.com. </p> 
           <p>Am I on the right track?</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1501#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1501&quot;, &quot;1501&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to megancarroll">Reply</a>

         <ul class="children"> 
          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1502"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-09-23T16:57:35+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1502" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">September 23, 2013 at 4:57 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Megan, that’s the process I’d use, with a couple notes: I would use a subdomain (newsite.example.com) rather than a subdirectory (example.com/newsite) to reduce the chances of the dev site being indexed by search engines. You could use a subdirectory if you configured your robots.txt file properly, but I’ve found that it’s easier to just put dev sites in subdomains. Also, after you duplicate the site, log into the dev site and in the Reading settings, check the box for <em>Discourage search engines from indexing this site</em>. Remember to uncheck this after you duplicate the dev site back to live.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">

I only had a couple problems, one I was working on a password protected dev sub domain so I had to make it public again for the transfer to work.</p> 
           <p>The other problem I could use some help with. On the new domain the “Â” character has shown up in multiple paragraphs throughout the site. Is there an easy way to remove them or do I have to go post by post and edit each of these errant characters out?</p>

          <div class="comment-reply">

         <ul class="children"> 
          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor even depth-2" id="comment-1512"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-10-14T14:07:58+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1512" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">October 14, 2013 at 2:07 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Sean, it sounds like the database character set changed. Open your wp-config.php file for each site (original and copy), and compare the values for <code><a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Editing_wp-config.php#Database_character_set" rel="nofollow">define( 'DB_CHARSET'</a></code>. If the copy is different than the original, change it to match, then check the site again. If that doesn’t work, you may need to <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Converting_Database_Character_Sets" rel="nofollow">convert the copy’s database to a different character set</a>. I haven’t done this, but hopefully that Codex page helps. There may be plugins that do it too.</p> 
             <p>When you find the solution, please post it here. I’m sure others would appreciate the follow-up.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1512#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1512&quot;, &quot;1512&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Chad Warner">Reply</a>

              <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
               <p>Hi there,</p> 
               <p>I had this same problem. For some reason I found that when changing changing ‘utf8’ to ‘utf-8? (hence the “dash”), all of the weird “A” character’s were gone. Note, this is located just after define (‘DB_CHARSET’) function.</p> 
               <p>Hope this helps.</p> 
               <p>Sara</p> 
              </div>

             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-10-15T11:08:56+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1514" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">October 15, 2013 at 11:08 am</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Kay, that could be happening for several reasons. Here are some places to check for redirects: domain registrar, DNS host, hosting panel (such as cPanel), .htaccess file, and a redirect plugin in WordPress. If you don’t see redirects in any of those places, you may need to ask your host or system admin for help.</p>

The WordPress Codex has some good articles about moving WordPress and changing site URLs: <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Moving_WordPress" rel="nofollow">Moving WordPress</a>, <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Giving_WordPress_Its_Own_Directory" rel="nofollow">Giving WordPress Its Own Directory</a>, and <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Changing_The_Site_URL" rel="nofollow">Changing The Site URL</a>. Each article covers several different scenarios, so see the table of contents.</p>

           <p>Hi Chad,</p> 
           <p>Have you ever encountered issues with adding a duplicated WordPress site into a sub directory? I followed everything properly; however, when clicking on ‘test connection’ within the installer setup, I receive the following error:</p> 
           <p>“INSTALL ERROR!<br> The database “mydatabasename” has 15 tables. The Duplicator only works with an EMPTY database. Enable the “Table Removal” checkbox to delete all tables and proceed with installation. Please backup all your data before proceeding!</p> 
           <p>Some hosting providers do not allow table removal from scripts like the Duplicator. In this case you will need to login to your hosting providers control panel and remove the tables manually. Please contact your hosting provider for further details.”</p> 
           <p>I don’t dare empty the database as I’m assuming that the database its referring to is the one that enables the main website to function (considering that’s the mySQL info I typed in in order to be accepted)…all I’m seeking to do is be able to work on a WordPress site in a ‘testing’ area to see how it looks before making those changes on the live site. I don’t want to mess with any files that affect the main website though.</p> 
           <p>Any ideas on this would be amazing! I’ve found nothing online so far…</p> 
           <p>Thanks!!<br> Melissa</p>

           <p>So I got the Duplicator process down. I now have my website.dev on my computer that is a copy of production so I can test out some styling and what not. One thing I’m having trouble finding a clear explanation is how to push updates from your developer site to production. Looking for suggestions or a nice process to make that happen.           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1538"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-12-26T11:14:21+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1538" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">December 26, 2013 at 11:14 am</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>I usually duplicate the entire dev site back to production, or move just the relevant part(s) (new theme, etc.). I haven’t needed anything more sophisticated, so I haven’t looked for options. I’ve heard that <a href="http://deliciousbrains.com/wp-migrate-db-pro/" rel="nofollow">WP Migrate DB Pro</a> is great for keeping WordPress databases in sync, but I haven’t used it. If you come across any other good tools or techniques, please comment again.</p>

Regarding files, you will need to delete the WordPress files from the directory into which you want to duplicate the site. Be sure you have a copy of those files before deleting them! If you need more help, please see the Troubleshooting section near the end of the post.</p>

          <li class="comment odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1553"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/dd8a7951ddc458f9e92259a96cabdf4d?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/dd8a7951ddc458f9e92259a96cabdf4d?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://easywebdesigntutorials.com/" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Paal Joachim Romdahl</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-01-28T09:23:01+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1553" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">January 28, 2014 at 9:23 am</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Hi Melissa</p> 
             <p>Place the installer.php file and the Duplicator zip package into the root/folder where you plan on adding a new site. </p> 
             <p>There is an option in the beginning to Create new or remove all tables. You want to remove all the tables of the existing database WordPress site. When you got to step 2 a message will come up that says that you have to delete the existing sites wp-config.php file. When that is done then you can install the new site on top of the existing site.</p> 
             <p>I have created a New video tutorial for the new 0.5.0 version:<br> <a href="http://easywebdesigntutorials.com/wordpress/duplicator-tutorial-videos/" rel="nofollow">http://easywebdesigntutorials.com/wordpress/duplicator-tutorial-videos/</a></p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1553#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1553&quot;, &quot;1553&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Paal Joachim Romdahl">Reply</a>

        <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-1542"> 
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
          <header class="comment-header"> 
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/91a3285bfd7df5dc0742e21c04cd03b0?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/91a3285bfd7df5dc0742e21c04cd03b0?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name">Melissa</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-01-09T20:06:36+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1542" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">January 9, 2014 at 8:06 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>Great, thanks Chad! I ended up pulling someone else to help me on it as it was a bit complicated. </p> 
           <p>First thing, turn off the permalinks in WordPress on the new ‘sub directory’ site (select default and hit save). Also in WordPress under settings – general, change the ‘site address url’ to reflect the root url (remove the ‘/duplicated site’). After this one has to ‘drop’ the files within the root website database through phpMyAdmin. For the other database – the new one, there is software you have to run – a search and replace software (Search-Replace-DB-3.0.0), where you search for any instances of ‘/yoursite/duplicated site/’ on the database that was created for the sub directory site, replacing it with the root url – so just ‘/yoursite/’. After that software works its magic, you export the files from that database, and import them into the newly emptied root website database. After this, through an FTP client or using your cPanel, you clear the ‘wp-content’ folder on the root drive and add the ‘wp-content’ folder as well as ‘wp-config.php’ from the new site that was created. Everything should work fine. Remember to check the permalinks through the WordPress admin panel to ensure that they’e back on.</p> 
           <p>It was impossible to find this info anywhere so hopefully this helps someone else.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1542#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1542&quot;, &quot;1542&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Melissa">Reply</a>
          </div>

             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-01-09T20:13:04+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1543" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">January 9, 2014 at 8:13 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Melissa, I’m glad you got it figured out. Without seeing your WordPress installation I can’t say for sure, but that sounds a lot more complicated than it should be. Duplicator should be able to handle permalinks, changing the site URL, and unpackaging the WordPress directories (wp-content, etc.). I may have had to use the <a href="https://wordpress.org/plugins/search-and-replace/" rel="nofollow">Search and Replace plugin</a> in some rare instances, but otherwise Duplicator usually does almost everything else.</p> 
             <p>In any case, I’m glad your migration worked. Thank you for your detailed comments. I’m sure others will benefit from your experience.</p> 
            </div>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>Hello everyone!</p> 
           <p>Duplicator has a new developer version which also does basic multisite, has a rewritten backend and more.</p> 
           <p>Browse to <a href="https://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/duplicator/developers/" rel="nofollow">http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/duplicator/developers/</a><br> Look for the section “Other Versions”<br> Click on “Development Version” and download the zip plugin file<br> Uninstall your current version and install this one</p> 
           <p>Here is an overview of the changes:<br> <a href="https://lifeinthegrid.com/support/knowledgebase.php?article=20" rel="nofollow">https://lifeinthegrid.com/support/knowledgebase.php?article=20</a></p> 
           <p>If you can test it out that would be great!<br> If you find any bugs please do submit them here:<br> <a href="https://lifeinthegrid.com/support" rel="nofollow">https://lifeinthegrid.com/support</a></p> 
           <p>Have a great weekend!</p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1551"> 
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
          <header class="comment-header"> 
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/f40e08a95c2b567e5256c0ac0af3512b?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/f40e08a95c2b567e5256c0ac0af3512b?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name">Murray</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-01-27T20:53:08+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1551" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">January 27, 2014 at 8:53 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>I spent days with to get Duplicator going. It downloaded more or less empty sites ok but I could not get the package created with a larger site. I stripped out everything I could and it was about 120MB. However it would always timeout and unfortunately the host, (Vodahost) would not change that as they said it was a security risk. </p> 
           <p>I have had extensive communications with the developers (see on WordPress.org forum) but could not get it working. Neither did I have access to change Open Dir settings. I also tried XCloner but met up with similar issues. I am now on the lookout for a tool to speed up with moving a live site to a local site. </p> 
           <p>I suspect many users with shared hosting will run into similar problems. A pity.</p> 
          </div>

            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Murray, thanks for sharing your experience. Shared hosts often have tight resource limits, hampering plugins like Duplicator. If you can’t find a plugin that works in your situation, you may need to manually move the database and files by using tools such as phpMyAdmin and FTP. See <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Moving_WordPress" rel="nofollow">Moving WordPress</a> in the Codex for more info.</p>

             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-02-18T06:24:10+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1556" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">February 18, 2014 at 6:24 am</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>If you duplicated the site successfully, and don’t need to duplicate it again within the next few days, you should deactivate and delete Duplicator. By default, it will remove its settings and delete the wp-snapshots folder when you do so. By removing plugins that aren’t actively being used, you make your site more secure, because there’s less code for hackers to exploit.</p> 
            </div>

             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>

            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Yes, Mike, you can use Duplicator to make a copy of the site at a new host with a new domain name. If much of the content will be identical between both sites, you should research <a href="https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/66359?hl=en" rel="nofollow">Google’s stance on duplicate content</a> (they generally frown on it). See also <a href="http://moz.com/learn/seo/duplicate-content" rel="nofollow">What is Duplicate Content? by Moz</a>. I’m not an SEO specialist, but I can put you in touch with a couple if you’d like more info on that.</p> 
            </div>

Yes, it will be a copy of your site as it was at the old domain. Duplicator copies the WordPress database and files. You will be able to work with WordPress as usual.</p>

           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-04-30T12:11:39+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1564" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">April 30, 2014 at 12:11 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>For anyone getting the “WP-CONFIG WARNING: The wp-config.php has one or more of these values ….. error, simply open wp-config and comment out the following:</p> 
           <p>/*—-define(‘WP_SITEURL’, ‘……..’ . $_SERVER[‘HTTP_HOST’] . ‘/wordpress’);<br> define(‘WP_HOME’, ‘………’ . $_SERVER[‘HTTP_HOST’] . ‘/wordpress’);—–*/</p> 
           <p>It worked for me.</p> 
          </div>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1565">

          <header class="comment-header"> 
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/722107e6a8154a0eadeb185c5d9b4efa?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/722107e6a8154a0eadeb185c5d9b4efa?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://kirksmith-novelist.com/blog" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">May May Gong</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-04-30T16:39:59+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1565" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">April 30, 2014 at 4:39 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>We are trying to merge a standalone blog (let’s call it the-Blog.com) into another website. The goal is to have the contents of the blog display in the website like so: the-website.com/blog</p> 
           <p>I used the duplicator plugin and it worked great! Created a folder within the website called ‘blog’ and uploaded what duplicator copied. Voila — there it is — sort of! : )</p> 
           <p>On what was the blog’s homepage, the main content no longer displays, but shows a 404 Error. The sidebar, listing past posts and comments, still displays just fine — BUT — they still have the URL for the separate standalone blog, i.e. the-Blog.com.</p> 
           <p>I’m drawing a blank what to do here — I’m assuming it’s do-able to have the blog content now display under the URL of the website? Thanks for the great tutorial. We are 80% there, I think.</p>

            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-04-30T17:59:25+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1566" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">April 30, 2014 at 5:59 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>What you’re trying to achieve has more to do with configuring WordPress than with Duplicator. I haven’t done what you’re attempting, so I can’t give any specific guidance. You might need to <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Changing_The_Site_URL" rel="nofollow">change the WordPress Address and/or Site Address</a> in the General Settings of your imported site (the blog), either after importing, or as part of the import process with Duplicator. You might also consider running both sites inside a <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Create_A_Network" rel="nofollow">WordPress Network</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1566#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1566&quot;, &quot;1566&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Chad Warner">Reply</a>

           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-06-25T20:28:00+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1574" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">June 25, 2014 at 8:28 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>I’m glad the post was helpful. I haven’t dealt with a character set problem in a long time. I think I solved one once by adding the default <code>define( 'DB_CHARSET', 'utf8' );</code> to a wp-config.php that was missing it. See <a href="https://codex.wordpress.org/Editing_wp-config.php#Database_character_set" rel="nofollow">Database character set</a> in the Codex. There are a couple of old, inactive plugins that may be worth trying: <a href="https://wordpress.org/plugins/utf-8-database-converter/" rel="nofollow">UTF-8 Database Converter</a> and <a href="https://wordpress.org/plugins/utf-8-db-converter/" rel="nofollow">Convert WP Database to UTF-8</a>. Otherwise, try the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/" rel="nofollow">WordPress support forums</a> or <a href="https://wordpress.stackexchange.com/" rel="nofollow">wordpress.stackexchange.com</a>.</p> 
             <p>If you figure it out, please post another comment with your findings.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">

                <header class="comment-header"> 
                 <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
                 <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-06-26T06:42:17+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1576" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">June 26, 2014 at 6:42 am</a></time></p> 
                </header> 
                <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
                 <p>You may need to change the characters directly in the database. I once followed the post <a href="https://digwp.com/2011/07/clean-up-weird-characters-in-database/" rel="nofollow">Clean Up Weird Characters in Database</a> with success. It’s an old post, but I suspect it still works. Start with the queries they show, then add your own to target the characters in your site. As always, make a backup first.</p>

          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor even depth-2" id="comment-1585"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-10-30T14:58:02+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1585" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">October 30, 2014 at 2:58 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Amit, if I understand your question, you want to duplicate to a <em>different</em> server, but keep the <em>domain</em> the same. In that case, I suggest using the <a href="https://wpengine.com/support/emulate-dns-change-with-the-hosts-file-trick/" rel="nofollow">hosts file trick</a> to point your domain to the IP address of the new server, then accessing domain.com/installer.php. When Duplicator asks for the new domain, use the same one. I’m just guessing at these steps because I haven’t done this with Duplicator before. But, I’ve done similar things with the BackupBuddy plugin.</p> 
             <p>If this doesn’t work, please seek support by following the links in the Troubleshooting section of this post.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">

          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1588"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-11-03T14:39:10+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1588" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">November 3, 2014 at 2:39 pm</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>You’re welcome, Justin. You may want to look into version control (such as <a href="https://git-scm.com/" rel="nofollow">Git</a>) and/or a database syncing tool, such as <a href="https://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-migrate-db/" rel="nofollow">WP Migrate DB</a> (or the <a href="https://deliciousbrains.com/wp-migrate-db-pro/" rel="nofollow">pro version</a>). We don’t provide support for any of these, but hopefully that sets you in the right direction. You can also try the <a href="https://wordpress.org/support/" rel="nofollow">WordPress.org support forums</a>.</p> 
            </div>

        <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-1589"> 
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
          <header class="comment-header"> 
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/39f557ec1f5c4759b6c4e846d12acd45?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/39f557ec1f5c4759b6c4e846d12acd45?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://martinaschwarz.net/" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">bryan james</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
           <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-11-09T14:40:49+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1589" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">November 9, 2014 at 2:40 pm</a></time></p> 
          </header> 
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>Interesting article, thank you for that. I’ve moved two wordpress sites with Duplicator, First one no problem whatsoever (I was moving it into the root directory). The second time, moving to another domain, it looked like it hadn’t worked as the installer gave me some MySQL error messages I couldn’t overcome. I read a tip saying to try extracting the package zip file (working in the folder in cPanel). </p> 
           <p>This actually worked, although I had to change a couple of files to reflect the new url. (just open any obvious ones, config.php, etc) So if the installer doesn’t work a bit of playing around with all the folder and files unzipped (essentially your saved website) should do the trick.</p> 
           <p>A final point, initially the whole menu structure had changed to something very clumsy, even though I could see it as created in the dashboard when I viewed it in ‘customize your site’. After hours of head-scratching, I deactivated W3 Total Cache and it miraculously reverted to how I’d designed it. For my next move, coming soon, I’m making a point to turn off all my plugins! It’s always a bit nerve-racking though!</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1589#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1589&quot;, &quot;1589&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to bryan james">Reply</a>
          </div>

          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chad bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1592"> 
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Comment"> 
            <header class="comment-header"> 
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Person"> <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d50b88f026bbac00217ca2858a30d630?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"><span itemprop="name"><a href="http://optimwise.com" class="comment-author-link" rel="external nofollow" itemprop="url">Chad Warner</a></span> <span class="says">says</span> </p> 
             <p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-12-11T06:02:48+00:00" itemprop="datePublished"><a href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/#comment-1592" class="comment-time-link" itemprop="url">December 11, 2014 at 6:02 am</a></time></p> 
            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Trevor, double-check that you have the index.php in the right directory on the server. Next, clear any caches between the web server and you (server-level, CDNs, browser, etc.). If you still get a 404 for the index.php URL, I suggest following the links in the Troubleshooting section of this post. When you solve the problem, please leave another comment with your solution, so others can benefit.</p>

            </header> 
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Jason, you should use FTP or your host’s file manager to upload the installer.php file to the destination directory on your new URL. Also make sure it’s named “installer.php” with nothing else in the filename. That way, yourdomain.com/installer.php will work. If it still doesn’t, clear any caches between the web server and you (server-level, CDNs, browser, etc.). If it still doesn’t work, I suggest following the links in the Troubleshooting section of this post. When you solve the problem, please leave another comment with your solution, so others can benefit.</p> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://optimwise.com/copy-migrate-wordpress-sites-with-the-duplicator-plugin/?replytocom=1605#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-1605&quot;, &quot;1605&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;2455&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Chad Warner">Reply</a>
            </div>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="text"> 
           <p>nice finding! I use a similar plugin which is called WordPress Backup to Dropbox. As the name says, it actually only offers to backup to Dropbox which is what I am fine with.</p> 
           <p>I have set it up to run once a day and besides the database it backs up everything located in the blog’s folder and what I didn’t exclude from backups.</p> 
           <p>I think in the end it doesn’t matter what product you use to to backups, as long as they are done and stored at a safe place. Too many people just rely on the backups offered by their hosting service.</p>

			if ( 'undefined' !== typeof addComment ) {
				addComment._Jetpack_moveForm = addComment.moveForm;

				addComment.moveForm = function( commId, parentId, respondId, postId ) {
					var returnValue = addComment._Jetpack_moveForm( commId, parentId, respondId, postId ), cancelClick, cancel;

					if ( false === returnValue ) {
						cancel = document.getElementById( 'cancel-comment-reply-link' );
						cancelClick = cancel.onclick;
						cancel.onclick = function() {
							var cancelReturn = cancelClick.call( this );
							if ( false !== cancelReturn ) {
								return cancelReturn;
							}

							if ( !comm_par ) {
								return cancelReturn;
							}

							comm_par = 0;

							tellFrameNewParent();

							return cancelReturn;
						};
					}

					if ( comm_par == parentId ) {
						return returnValue;
					}

					comm_par = parentId;

					tellFrameNewParent();

					return returnValue;
				};
			}
